  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_63ce6578-e02b-4089-ae38-0283c2a585cb'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer2608445296574917477"><b>The #1 <i>New York Times</i> Bestseller <i>You Are A Badass</i> is the self-help book for people who desperately want to improve their lives but don't want to get busted doing it.</b><br/><br/>In this refreshingly entertaining how-to guide, #1 <i>New York Times</i> Bestselling Author and world-traveling success coach, Jen Sincero, serves up 27 bite-sized chapters full of hilariously inspiring stories, sage </span>
  <span id="freeText2608445296574917477" style="display:none"><b>The #1 <i>New York Times</i> Bestseller <i>You Are A Badass</i> is the self-help book for people who desperately want to improve their lives but don't want to get busted doing it.</b><br /><br />In this refreshingly entertaining how-to guide, #1 <i>New York Times</i> Bestselling Author and world-traveling success coach, Jen Sincero, serves up 27 bite-sized chapters full of hilariously inspiring stories, sage advice, easy exercises, and the occasional swear word. If you're ready to make some serious changes around here, <i>You Are a Badass</i> will help you: Identify and change the self-sabotaging beliefs and behaviors that stop you from getting what you want, blast past your fears so you can take big exciting risks, figure out how to make some damn money already, learn to love yourself and others, set big goals and reach them - it will basically show you how to create a life you totally love, and how to create it <i>now</i>.<br /><br />By the end of <i>You Are a Badass</i>, you'll understand why you are how you are, how to love what you can't change, how to change what you don't love, and how to use The Force to kick some serious ass.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2608445296574917477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1340821789?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/1486808-karen">Karen</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1340821789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14995834769272684116">Not good. I can sum up this book pretty quickly. If you want to make a change in your life, or if you are not happy with your life, you are the only one who can make it better. There were a few things that really bothered me. If you are depressed, you cannot simply decide that you are not going to be depressed anymore and get yourself out and have fun. It is apparent that the author has never experienced depression, or been a very sympathetic friend to anyone she knows who has been depressed. I </span>
  <span id="freeText14995834769272684116" style="display:none">Not good. I can sum up this book pretty quickly. If you want to make a change in your life, or if you are not happy with your life, you are the only one who can make it better. There were a few things that really bothered me. If you are depressed, you cannot simply decide that you are not going to be depressed anymore and get yourself out and have fun. It is apparent that the author has never experienced depression, or been a very sympathetic friend to anyone she knows who has been depressed. I also feel that some of her advice is not very practical in the real world. So if I'm a single mom supporting 4-5 kids, and I've always dreamed of starting my own business, I should just quit my job? I should buy expensive things, that I might not be able to pay for? There is some good advice on stopping negative thoughts, but some of the examples of going for what you really want are just not practical for most people.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1771337714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1771337714" />
    <a title="Laura Bradbury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23241429-laura-bradbury"><img alt="Laura Bradbury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420684864p2/23241429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1771337714?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Bradbury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Bradbury" href="/user/show/23241429-laura-bradbury">Laura Bradbury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23241429-laura-bradbury?shelf=zenish-spiritual-new-age">zenish-spiritual-new-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1771337714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13652327873424213171">*** PSA: Vent Alert***<br/><br/>I didn't give this review a low rating because Sicero is a bad writer - she is perfectly effective for the task at hand and actually her appealing "ra-ra-go-get'em" voice is what drew me in to begin with. I ultimately bailed however, as I have a Big Problem with the central thesis of this book. Basically it all boils down to the theory that everyone has the power to "manifest" their own reality and if things are not working out for them it is because they are not manifestin</span>
  <span id="freeText13652327873424213171" style="display:none">*** PSA: Vent Alert***<br /><br />I didn't give this review a low rating because Sicero is a bad writer - she is perfectly effective for the task at hand and actually her appealing "ra-ra-go-get'em" voice is what drew me in to begin with. I ultimately bailed however, as I have a Big Problem with the central thesis of this book. Basically it all boils down to the theory that everyone has the power to "manifest" their own reality and if things are not working out for them it is because they are not manifesting hard enough and / or not "vibrating" at a high enough level. <br /><br />I completely understand the seductive draw of this philosophy i.e. we all control our own destiny. Wouldn't that be simple and lovely? The hard, cold truth - much less palatable to swallow- is that we do not. I do believe that we can choose our attitude most of the time, and that we can choose to give even difficult things in life meaning, but choose what actually happens to us? I'm calling bullshit. I don't buy it. <br /><br />You see, the dark underbelly of Sincero's philosophy is that - if taken to its logical conclusion - it blames the victims of misfortune. So...are children with terminal cancer just not manifesting hard enough? Was the generation of Jews brutally murdered in the Holocaust simply not vibrating at the right frequency? How do the manifesters / vibrators (there are many writers that espouse this theory - especially, I have noticed, those published by Hay House) explain that? Sometimes people are served up an unresolvable shit sandwich by life, and making them feel they should be vibrating and manifesting their way out of it kind of lacks humanity, you know?<br /><br />It's not like I am some sad sack sitting here at home spending my days feeling sorry for myself and the human race. I have done many things I consider rather badass things in my life - took off to France for a year when I was 17 and spoke zero French, applied and got accepted into Oxford University, bought and renovated four vacation rentals in Burgundy, wrote and self-published four bestselling books, and now I am dealing with a life-threatening medical condition (see above re: shit sandwich) in the most pro-active manner I know how...Nevertheless, my brand of bad-assery does not negate the reality that we don't control everything (much as this fact continues to annoy me). People should not be blamed for the curve balls that life lobs at their heads from time to time. They deserve our empathy and compassion, not to be made to feel as though their situation is their fault. Now go and try to manifest and vibrate your way out of that one! ;) <br /><br />***Vent Over*** <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13652327873424213171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15361889463886735159">I read one and a half chapters and then stumbled on the whole idea of source energy. If I want some real change in my life, I want real tips and not some esoteric mumbo jumbo. I'm also a bit peeved that the author mentioned in the very beginning that her readers should be open minded about her methods, and if they weren't they should just deal with living a sucky life. As if her methods were the only working ones.<br/>So I hardly have to mention that I stopped reading it immediately.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1203682175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1203682175" />
    <a title="Carolyn Francis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21474918-carolyn-francis"><img alt="Carolyn Francis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387656432p2/21474918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1203682175?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn Francis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn Francis" href="/user/show/21474918-carolyn-francis">Carolyn Francis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203682175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10464799103962647443">A friend, who will remain nameless for her personal safety, told me that this book changed her life. I am so very happy for her. What I took from Jen Sincero's self-help-memoir was: that I am most definitely not a "badass", that I'm really, really fine with that, and that reading about it did not make me want to "share my awesomeness with the world" so much as contemplate a life of violent crime. Please do not ever, ever read it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

Ms. Sincero identifies common thought processes and behaviors that keep us</span>
  <span id="freeText3240993579735601563" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447818671i/17054438.jpg" width="500" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>OMG, this book was so, so good. The message was exactly what I needed to hear. So much craziness is going on in my life right now and I find myself doubting my greatness every...single...day. <br><br>The point <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/69641.Jen_Sincero" title="Jen Sincero" rel="nofollow noopener">Jen Sincero</a> makes in this self-help book is we are all great, we all have enormous potential, we all possess the power to succeed at absolutely everything we direct our energy towards, but we are also our very own obstacle. Ms. Sincero identifies common thought processes and behaviors that keep us from living a truly awesome life and she coaches the reader on how to identify them, replace them, and move forward like a badass.<br><br>The first half of this book was absolutely perfect in my opinion - my favorite chapters were the ones about the power of gratitude. The later chapters got a little too new-age for my personal taste, with all the talk about the universe, vibrating energies, and controlling frequencies, but I could see where she was going with it. I benefited from this book and plan to implement some of the suggestions...I already have actually :). It really is great and I highly recommend it. Check it out!<br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br><i>“And while there are countless ways that we rip ourselves off, there’s one way in particular that is, without a doubt, the most rampant and the most devastating of all: we invest everything we’ve got in believing that we’re not good enough.”</i></span>

<div id="review_1748688276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1748688276" />
    <a title="Laura Hoffman Brauman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2597121-laura-hoffman-brauman"><img alt="Laura Hoffman Brauman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249442128p2/2597121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1748688276?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Hoffman Brauman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Hoffman Brauman" href="/user/show/2597121-laura-hoffman-brauman">Laura Hoffman Brauman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1748688276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17774017291495670338">I got the audio of this on sale and I love the title -- but that was the thing I loved the most about it. When I started listening to it, I thought -- okay, maybe a little too "woo-woo" for me, but the tone is fun and it moves quickly and the audio was the right length for the rest of my ride. As I kept listening, I decided it was ok, not great, but some useful tips. Decided I probably wouldn't review it since I don't usually do reviews if I don't have something positive to say. And then I got t</span>
  <span id="freeText17774017291495670338" style="display:none">I got the audio of this on sale and I love the title -- but that was the thing I loved the most about it. When I started listening to it, I thought -- okay, maybe a little too "woo-woo" for me, but the tone is fun and it moves quickly and the audio was the right length for the rest of my ride. As I kept listening, I decided it was ok, not great, but some useful tips. Decided I probably wouldn't review it since I don't usually do reviews if I don't have something positive to say. And then I got to a couple of sections that I thought gave advice that was downright irresponsible -- and decided I would review it. At one point, the author decided to buy a car that was way out of her price range because she fell in love with it. While I respect that this made her change some things in her work life to enable her to pay for a luxury car she couldn't afford, it is irresponsible to give this advice. Several times, she encouraged readers to use credit cards to purchase luxuries that they didn't have the money for if they saw these things as part of the life they envisioned for themselves. Her philosophy that you just need to "manifest" your thoughts about the money you need and you will attract it to you seemed dismissive of the true challenges of poverty. People aren't poor because they don't have good mental energy about money -- and thinking positively about money and vibrating at the right frequency isn't ending poverty. While some of the tips that she gave were useful and could help a reader make positive change in their life, there were enough areas where I thought her advice was overly simplified and ignored the realities that many face. I ended up getting pretty angry at some of her suggestions and tips.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17774017291495670338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Emmy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3457550-emmy"><img alt="Emmy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368455971p2/3457550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/678195347?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emmy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emmy" href="/user/show/3457550-emmy">Emmy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer678195347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9042809763112291899">This book was Badass!!!! If you have any mental barriers that are holding you back from achieving your goals then this book is for you! You have to be comfortable with some colorful language, and the idea of the Law of Attraction, but if you're open minded you will get a lot from this book. I've read a lot of books on this subject, but this one was so much more in your face (in a good way) and more easy to put into practice. I plan to read it again right away to make sure I get the full effect! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2246514627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2246514627" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2246514627?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall">2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2246514627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7418319160877656891">Served with a healthy dose of humor, a smidge of sarcasm and plenty of great quotes, <b> Jen Sincero dishes her take </b> on self-help, self- acceptance and (of course) <b>
  <i> self-love.</i>
</b><br/><br/>This has all the hallmarks of a Self-Help book - cheesy one-liners and a perky "You CAN do it" attitude. I honestly expected it to be just another cookie cutter how to become the <i>real</i> you. Bleh. Needless to say, <b>I was <i>totally</i> ready to hate it. </b> <br/><br/>Yet, the more I read, <b> the more I enjoyed hearing her advice. </b> She's hilarious</span>
  <span id="freeText7418319160877656891" style="display:none">Served with a healthy dose of humor, a smidge of sarcasm and plenty of great quotes, <b> Jen Sincero dishes her take </b> on self-help, self- acceptance and (of course) <b>
  <i> self-love.</i>
</b><br /><br />This has all the hallmarks of a Self-Help book - cheesy one-liners and a perky "You CAN do it" attitude. I honestly expected it to be just another cookie cutter how to become the <i>real</i> you. Bleh. Needless to say, <b>I was <i>totally</i> ready to hate it. </b> <br /><br />Yet, the more I read, <b> the more I enjoyed hearing her advice. </b> She's hilarious. She's witty. <b>And she's pretty badass.</b> There were quite a few quotes that articulated concepts that I never fully thought through before: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>If you’re serious about changing your life, you’ll find a way. If you’re not, you’ll find an excuse.<br /><br />You are responsible for what you say and do. You are not responsible for whether or not people freak out about it.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Her real life tie-ins and her examples were absolutely spot on. I <b> busted a gut</b> when she started calling out all those little excuses we tell ourselves:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> Sally always says She can't find a good single man because there aren't any left out there. Really Sally? All the good single men were hunted down and killed so no matter how many dates you go on or how many times you put on sexy high heels and hang around home depot, you'll never bump into one? Was the awesome guy your friend Deb just met the lone survivor of the Good Guy Genocide? </i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Absolutely hilarious from cover to cover.</b> <br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />--- Read by the author. She freaking nailed it. Great tone, great comedic timing. I loved the way she'd say all the funny a asides in her "attitude" voice. <br /><br /><i> The Finer Books Club - 2018 Reading Challenge: An audiobook read by the author</i><br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7418319160877656891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13241926071281653416">Technically I didn't finish this book. But I read 82% of it, all the while growing more and more unimpressed, until finally I got to the point that I just had to stop. My kindle says there's 33 minutes left for me to read. But I've decided I want those 33 minutes to myself.<br/><br/>This book is basically a regurgitation of all other self-help kind of writings but with a "fun and hip" tone, or something.   <span id="freeText13241926071281653416" style="display:none">Technically I didn't finish this book. But I read 82% of it, all the while growing more and more unimpressed, until finally I got to the point that I just had to stop. My kindle says there's 33 minutes left for me to read. But I've decided I want those 33 minutes to myself.<br /><br />This book is basically a regurgitation of all other self-help kind of writings but with a "fun and hip" tone, or something. Often this "devil may care" quality feels forced. There are some parts of this book that could be very useful to others, perhaps, but this was an exercise in annoying myself (and the author is very big on loving oneself, so clearly I wasn't learning from this book).<br /><br />I absolutely lost it, however, when the author basically says "buy a super expensive car that you can't afford (or your personal equivalent) because the money will magically appear!!!!" Exact quote: "I don't see the money, but I believe it's there and it will be mine dammit!"<br /><br />I'm all for the power of positive thinking but god damn if this isn't some incredibly privileged bullshit.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

    <a title="Dóri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48761581-d-ri"><img alt="Dóri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577546274p2/48761581.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2062035625?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dóri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dóri" href="/user/show/48761581-d-ri">Dóri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2062035625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2270327862810214594">I don't think any book has ever annoyed me like this one and that's saying something. I pushed through only because I wanted to check it off of my TBR. And because I was listening to it and didn't have anything else to listen to, so it was convinient while cleaning. Though.. There were times when I actually sad 'SHUT UP!' out loud because she was saying so ignorant bullshits.<br/><br/>1.) No, I don't have a low amount of money because I am afraid of it or hate it. We're actually quite good friends.<br/>2.) No,</span>
  <span id="freeText2270327862810214594" style="display:none">I don't think any book has ever annoyed me like this one and that's saying something. I pushed through only because I wanted to check it off of my TBR. And because I was listening to it and didn't have anything else to listen to, so it was convinient while cleaning. Though.. There were times when I actually sad 'SHUT UP!' out loud because she was saying so ignorant bullshits.<br /><br />1.) No, I don't have a low amount of money because I am afraid of it or hate it. We're actually quite good friends.<br />2.) No, I won't buy a luxury car that I can't afford just because I want to believe I have the money.<br />3.) No, I wont quit my secure well-paying job (if I'll have one) just to start my dream company when I have no capital. NO, I WON'T TAKE ON CREDIT FOR THAT EITHER! Especially not when I'll have a family to take care of as well.<br /><br />You get the point. And don't get me wrong, I totally believe in the law of attraction and yes, it does work for me, but what she recommends in this book is most of the time just downright irresponsible. <br /><br />I went into this book with high hopes and then I started reading some reviews, which were mostly negative, but I did find some positive ones and I always like to form my own opinion, so I decided to listen to it anyways, this time with lower hopes. Well, the first few minutes it managed to get on my nerves. I don't remember the exact quote, but she said something like this: 'You can decide to either listen to this book and take my advice or you can go back to your sucky life.' Seriously??! First off, I did not say I had a sucky life, so do not suppose stuff and write them in a book. Second of all, I kind of regret sticking here listening to your 'advice' rather than coming back to my 'sucky' life.<br /><br />So, what I'm trying to say here is that you do not insult the reader, that's not what makes a book good. What makes a book good is that it's original, not full of clichés, not repetative, not giving advice that can make people broke and go bankrupt, and most importantly, you do not talk like the reader is completely ignorant!<br /><br />I don't want to go on and on about how much I hated this book, so probably it's for the best that I stop right here because you probably already understood the message I was trying to send.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2270327862810214594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2105791320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2105791320" />
    <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn"><img alt="Skyler Autumn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534857879p2/12859342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2105791320?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skyler Autumn" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn">Skyler Autumn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2105791320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15575977168127804263"><b> 4 Stars </b><br/><br/>Jen Sincero is a badass who woke up from her mundane existence (THE BIG SNOOZE) and began throwing all her money, time and energy into the process of getting her true life back on track. <br/><br/>This book is like the cliff notes or the cheat sheet to all self help books everywhere. Which is why I loved it!! Instead of drawing out the formula to spirituality and meditation she gives you snippets of doable and less intimidating passages. This helps you take the beginning steps toward your badass-</span>
  <span id="freeText15575977168127804263" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars </b><br /><br />Jen Sincero is a badass who woke up from her mundane existence (THE BIG SNOOZE) and began throwing all her money, time and energy into the process of getting her true life back on track. <br /><br />This book is like the cliff notes or the cheat sheet to all self help books everywhere. Which is why I loved it!! Instead of drawing out the formula to spirituality and meditation she gives you snippets of doable and less intimidating passages. This helps you take the beginning steps toward your badass-ary instead of feeling overwhelmed by information and running in the opposite direction. <br /><br />Jen Sincero is not reinventing the wheel when it comes to the tried and true methods of getting out your own way and opening yourself up to possibilities of life. Which she is fully aware of, she's just giving you a simplified beginners guide to stop with the excuse and start making the changes you need TODAY! <br /><br />This book is a fountain of wisdom and QUOTES!! I love me some inspirational quotes! <i>Some of my faves are as followed; We only get to be in our bodies for a limit of time why not celebrate the journey instead of waiting out the ride or There is nothing more unstoppable then a frate train of FUCK YA! Or In order to kick ones ass you have to be willing to lift up your foot.</i><br /><br />All the passages really resonate with me; meditation, spirituality, gratitude, body scans, and the power of manifesting your true life. I will definitely use this book in my future as a reference guide to getting my shit together. <br /><br />Why the 4 stars if I'm preaching this books praise? Well like I said originality is not something you will find in this book but I appreciate the authors self- awareness that it is just reiterated knowledge that's already out there in the self help world. And frankly the money passage didn't resonate with me. Talking about the fear we have toward having money? I was like who fears having money!!!??? I fear I'm not gonna have enough money but I definitely don't fear having it! <br /><br />All and all read this book if you want a kick in the ass with a side of inspiration and bravado. I'm going to take some of Jen Sincero advice and apply it to my life now! What's the worse that could happen? I actually put myself out there and succeed! Sounds good to me : )</span>
  <a data-text-id="15575977168127804263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3435801980?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/155663-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/155663-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/155663-david?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3435801980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6373476813760990808">This book might be helpful to some people. But to me, when I hear sentences like the following:<br/>"All of us are connected to this limitless power, and most of us aren't using but a fraction of it"<br/><br/>or<br/><br/>"The universe is made up of source energy. All energy vibrates at a certain frequency, which means you're vibrating at a certain frequency, and everything you desire and don't desire is also vibrating at a certain frequency. Vibration attracts like vibration. Otherwise known as the law of attraction."<br/><br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText6373476813760990808" style="display:none">This book might be helpful to some people. But to me, when I hear sentences like the following:<br />"All of us are connected to this limitless power, and most of us aren't using but a fraction of it"<br /><br />or<br /><br />"The universe is made up of source energy. All energy vibrates at a certain frequency, which means you're vibrating at a certain frequency, and everything you desire and don't desire is also vibrating at a certain frequency. Vibration attracts like vibration. Otherwise known as the law of attraction."<br /><br />I get the feeling that this is a pop-psychology self-help book that is just using buzz words. Some people love this sort of "feel-good" self-help blather, but I do not.</span>

<div id="review_945765252" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/945765252" />
    <a title="Julie Ehlers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2120450-julie-ehlers"><img alt="Julie Ehlers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446217915p2/2120450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/945765252?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Ehlers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Ehlers" href="/user/show/2120450-julie-ehlers">Julie Ehlers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2120450-julie-ehlers?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer945765252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5314301449156558107">Page 238: <i>Hang out with people who are kicking ass and will make you feel like a giant loser if you're not kicking ass, too. I (obviously) can't stress this enough.</i><br/><br/>NOW you tell me.<br/><br/>I'm not a fan of "tough love." I understand it's necessary in some situations, but for example, if I were on <i>The Biggest Loser</i>, there is NO WAY I would choose the personal trainer who bellows and screams at everyone as if she's lost her marbles. That sort of thing would make me angry but it wouldn't really motivate me.</span>
  <span id="freeText5314301449156558107" style="display:none">Page 238: <i>Hang out with people who are kicking ass and will make you feel like a giant loser if you're not kicking ass, too. I (obviously) can't stress this enough.</i><br /><br />NOW you tell me.<br /><br />I'm not a fan of "tough love." I understand it's necessary in some situations, but for example, if I were on <i>The Biggest Loser</i>, there is NO WAY I would choose the personal trainer who bellows and screams at everyone as if she's lost her marbles. That sort of thing would make me angry but it wouldn't really motivate me. One thing I hated about <i>You Are a Badass</i> is that Jen Sincero works really hard to make you feel like a big loser if you haven't yet achieved every single dream you've ever had in life. I didn't find it motivating, I found it demoralizing and depressing. And I didn't even realize she was doing it deliberately until I got to the excerpt above. I wish I'd known it was intentional all along—I <i>still</i> wouldn't have found it motivating, but at least I would have been annoyed or angry instead of feeling like a giant loser the whole time.<br /><br />Beyond that, this book was <i>way</i> more woo-woo than I was expecting. Sincero believes very strongly that we need to "vibrate at a high frequency" and this will cause good things to come our way. Of course, we also need to work really hard, keep our eyes on the prize, and possibly wait years and years for those good things, which makes you wonder if the vibrating part is actually necessary. But it is! Be vibrating at a high frequency at all times or you have only yourself to blame if your life isn't amazing every minute! If you're not put off by this oft-repeated bit of woo-woo, just wait until you see the out-there books she recommends in the suggested reading at the back. Frankly, if I'd known this was what I was signing up for, I never would have bought this book in the first place. (Don't ask me why I <i>did</i> buy this book in the first place, because I don't remember.)<br /><br />As for what I liked about it. I know a lot of people are against self-help books on principle, but I'm not—people sometimes need advice, and as book people it makes sense we might turn to books. The only reason I've read so few self-help books myself is that most of them are deadly boring. But this one wasn't! It was well-written and lively and way funnier than any other self-help book I've tried. So at least I was entertained while feeling like a loser.<br /><br />Also, sometimes it's just good to get a reminder that thinking positively is a better idea than thinking negatively. I'm looking to make some big changes in my life, but I know it's going to be hard and a lot of work, and I've just been feeling depressed about it. This book reminded me that, even if things don't work out exactly as you want them to, you make things much easier on yourself simply by trying to have a good attitude instead of a poor one. I realize this is an obvious point, but it was something I did need to hear right now. In that sense this book was helpful.<br /><br />As I was getting close to finishing this book I was thinking I'd leave it in the lobby of my apartment building or my workplace's book swap rather than keeping it, but then I realized I'd done so much underlining in the book it would be a little weird to give it away. So that's where I'm at with this book—I apparently found a lot of meaning in it but still saw it as disposable. Should you read it? I think you all know whether this sort of thing appeals to you or not, and if it doesn't, this won't be the book that changes your mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5314301449156558107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7858793-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546468430p2/7858793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353099596?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/7858793-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7858793-alex?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353099596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14962395692057518746">I saw this at the airport in St. Louis and liked its affirmation that I was, indeed, a badass, so I decided to check it out from the library when I got back home. Honestly, who buys books at airports anymore? So expensive.<br/><br/>Now, this book would have me believe that it doesn't matter that this book is expensive, because if I truly feel that money will manifest itself in my future, then so it shall be. While I like the unbridled optimism that Sincero brings to this kinda half-baked self-help book, I</span>
  <span id="freeText14962395692057518746" style="display:none">I saw this at the airport in St. Louis and liked its affirmation that I was, indeed, a badass, so I decided to check it out from the library when I got back home. Honestly, who buys books at airports anymore? So expensive.<br /><br />Now, this book would have me believe that it doesn't matter that this book is expensive, because if I truly feel that money will manifest itself in my future, then so it shall be. While I like the unbridled optimism that Sincero brings to this kinda half-baked self-help book, I've never been able to get behind advice of that nature. It's much too easy for the advice-giver to say, "Well, you're just not doing it right" when my excessive faith-having turns me into a social exile. I'm down with taking a positive spin on life, believing that I deserve happiness, and all that crap--it's gotten me pretty far, actually--so good job, book.<br /><br />Despite its inherent gooshyness, <i>You Are A Badass</i> did reinforce some ideas that I already had about my role in my own happiness, and it did give me a few new epiphanies to chew on, which made it a successful self-help book. <br /><br />I just wanted to punch it in the face sometimes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14962395692057518746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6613702081167512633">Badasses SO rule!<br/><br/>I don't know why or how or wtf but this book was actually unexpectedly good. <br/><br/>While most of the ideas were not all that new, still the end result was astonishingly motivating. I think I just clicked with this book.<br/><br/>Q:<br/>There’s nothing as unstoppable as a freight train full of fuck-yeah. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>You're here. I'm here. I love you. I'm gonna pee all over the floor about it. (c) Ewww!<br/>Q:<br/>The only failure is quitting. Everything else is just gathering information. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>You cut yourself off fr</span>
  <span id="freeText6613702081167512633" style="display:none">Badasses SO rule!<br /><br />I don't know why or how or wtf but this book was actually unexpectedly good. <br /><br />While most of the ideas were not all that new, still the end result was astonishingly motivating. I think I just clicked with this book.<br /><br />Q:<br />There’s nothing as unstoppable as a freight train full of fuck-yeah. (c)<br />Q:<br />You're here. I'm here. I love you. I'm gonna pee all over the floor about it. (c) Ewww!<br />Q:<br />The only failure is quitting. Everything else is just gathering information. (c)<br />Q:<br />You cut yourself off from the supply of awesomeness when you are not in a state of gratitude. (c)<br />Q:<br />You are powerful. You are loved. You are surrounded by miracles. (c)<br />Q:<br />What other people think of you has nothing to do with you and everything to do with them. (c)<br />Q:<br />Because so often when we say we’re unqualified for something, what we’re really saying is that we’re too scared to try it, not that we can’t do it. (c)<br />Q:<br />The definition of screwing someone over is taking their money and doing a lousy job or destroying their water source or enslaving populations, things like that—your mother being disappointed or your father disapproving or your friends being outraged does not qualify as screwing someone over. (c)<br />Q:<br />The Universe is totally freaking out about how awesome you are. It’s got you wrapped in a warm gorilla hug of adoration. It wants to give you everything you desire. It wants you to be happy. It wants you to see what it sees in you. (c)<br />Q:<br />It never ceases to amaze me the precious time we spend chasing the squirrels around our brains, playing out our dramas, worrying about unwanted facial hair, seeking adoration, justifying our actions, complaining about slow Internet connections, dissecting the lives of idiots, when we are sitting in the middle of a full-blown miracle that is happening right here, right now. (c)<br />Q:<br />Never apologize for who you are. It lets the whole world down. (c)<br />Q:<br />We only get to be in our bodies for a limited time, why not celebrate the journey instead of merely riding it out until it’s over? (c)<br />Q:<br />Your life is your party. You get to choose how you invite people and experiences and things into it. (c)<br />Q:<br />You are perfect. To think anything less is as pointless as a river thinking that it’s got too many curves or that it moves too slowly or that its rapids are too rapid. (c)<br />Q:<br />All this is to say that it’s not your fault that you’re fucked up. It’s your fault if you stay fucked up... (c)<br />Q:<br />Say nice things about your body, dress it up, and take it out. Give it hot sex, luxurious baths, and massages. Move it, stretch it, nourish it, hydrate it, pay attention to it—The better our bodies feel, the happier and more productive we are. (c)<br />Q:<br />In order to kick ass you must first lift up your foot. (c)<br />Q:<br />There’s something called the Crab Effect. If you put a bunch of crabs in a bowl and if, while they’re in there crawling all over each other, one of them tries to climb out, the rest of them will try to pull him back down instead of helping to push him out. No wonder they’re called crabs. (c)<br />Q:<br />If you’re always late, start being early. (c)<br />Q:<br />... blurter of brilliance ... (c)</span>

<div id="review_1618570222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618570222" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1618570222?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=award-various">award-various</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-memoir-biography">genre-memoir-biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-how-to-self-help">genre-how-to-self-help</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-mature">bage-mature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-nonfiction">genre-nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-spiritual">genre-spiritual</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618570222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7653844682521566885">She molded these ideas into a brassy way of handing them out. It's perfect for the culture right now. Stand up and believe in yourself.<br/><br/>There is nothing new in here. Jen Sincero has learned all these lessons from other self-help styled books and cultures about manifesting our world. Most people are looking to be a badass it seems so this appeals to most people. She did a wonderful job packaging all these ideas. <br/><br/>The basic thrust of this idea is that our thoughts create our world to some extent and</span>
  <span id="freeText7653844682521566885" style="display:none">She molded these ideas into a brassy way of handing them out. It's perfect for the culture right now. Stand up and believe in yourself.<br /><br />There is nothing new in here. Jen Sincero has learned all these lessons from other self-help styled books and cultures about manifesting our world. Most people are looking to be a badass it seems so this appeals to most people. She did a wonderful job packaging all these ideas. <br /><br />The basic thrust of this idea is that our thoughts create our world to some extent and for most people, our self-doubt does get in our way. When we let our insecurities rule, it can be difficult to think we deserve something and so we end up sabotaging ourselves. I do think the problem with these lines of thinking is it comes down to wanting a lot of money, nothing wrong with that. <br /><br />I enjoy the story because I do need to get out of my own way. My negativity really has me down right now. I feel like I'm under a net of all the reasons I can't do something instead of reaching for what I want anyway. <br /><br />The thing is, most of her stories she says, she talks about the universe helping her out, but her friend set are well-off people who have means. If a person is in a low class and all the people they know have little means, this mind-set becomes more difficult and you have to work harder to have things work so quickly for you. This is easier if you are in a higher class as there is more mobility, but that doesn't mean it isn't possible. <br /><br />This book is in the vein of 7 Habits of Highly Effective People or 'The Secret' and other books. <br /><br />The point is that this is a technique to change the inner workings of a person. Change the inside, the only thin we really can change, and you can create more in life. I really do believe that. I still need the reminder. I need to find a way to live this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7653844682521566885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845931412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12077266481196613141">*****The full review of this book can be read at <a href='http://darlingandcompany.blogspot.com/2017/01/you-are-badass-by-jen-sincero.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darling & Co.</a>*****<br/><br/>I was really excited for this book. I have the day-by-day calendar and I love it. It's posts are quick and witty and there's a bonus on the back of every day that tells you something interesting, or is a little puzzle, or something to get you thinking. It's great. The book version was...a let down, for a few reasons.<br/><br/>Between the repetitiveness, Jen insulting the reader, and the big one, talking more about herself than actually how</span>
  <span id="freeText12077266481196613141" style="display:none">*****The full review of this book can be read at <a href="http://darlingandcompany.blogspot.com/2017/01/you-are-badass-by-jen-sincero.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Darling &amp; Co.</a>*****<br /><br />I was really excited for this book. I have the day-by-day calendar and I love it. It's posts are quick and witty and there's a bonus on the back of every day that tells you something interesting, or is a little puzzle, or something to get you thinking. It's great. The book version was...a let down, for a few reasons.<br /><br />Between the repetitiveness, Jen insulting the reader, and the big one, talking more about herself than actually how to help a person be a badass, the whole book was a disappointment. I don't know, maybe I'm already a badass and that's why I didn't like it; but I really didn't learn anything new from this book that I haven't read/heard a million times before.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y4Lvc+6sJJo8LEyYo4kuOaiVd7GTLrnywYw5Z/tr54HJJHR5tS+GoQJlbNQDngCGeAg5X6T/bsA76m5/jUKb3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ts49MA6mz89e5090DhXbAaveufdGW7tJu9CCrMFDoSzkaKY6VSVt9GCubziuAvW+e0P3GXGKbHtBttW0t2rdcA==')})

This book was wonderful education for people, education in how to live life effectively and get closer to the ideal of being a ‘success’ in life.But not everyone understands Stephen Covey’s model fully well, or maybe there are some people who haven’t read it yet. This is definitely true because we still see so much failure all around us. The first problem is that most people are too lazy to implement the ideals of Stephen Covey in their lives. They consider his masterpiece of a book as a mere coffee-table book or a book that you use for light reading when you are traveling and then forget all about it. They do not realize that this book contains life-changing information. Or, they take the information and do not make the effort to actually utilize it so that it becomes knowledge for them.The second problem is that a lot of people have a myopic view of Covey’s ideals. These are people who are impressed by the book already. If you ask them what the seven habits are, they can rattle them off end to end, but then they miss the larger picture. They do not understand that Covey was trying to tell more than he wrote in words. There are hidden implications in this book, yes, and a lot of people have just failed to see through them.That is what we are trying to do. We are trying to show you how Covey’s book, or rather, his model, was a complete model in itself. There was nothing amiss about it. If you implement it, there should be no aspect of your life that should go untouched. The only thing is that you have to understand these ideals and try to implement them in your life.But, before we barge into that area, it is extremely important to understand what these ideals are. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14829490787236018267">Jen Sincero is a #1 New York Times Bestselling author, speaker and success coach who has helped countless people transform their personal and professional lives via her public appearances, private sessions, coaching seminars and, most recently, her latest #1 NY Times Bestselling book, "You Are a Badass: How to Stop Doubting Your Greatness and Start Living an Awesome Life".<br/><br/>She’s spoken on stages al</span>
  <span id="freeText14829490787236018267" style="display:none">Jen Sincero is a #1 New York Times Bestselling author, speaker and success coach who has helped countless people transform their personal and professional lives via her public appearances, private sessions, coaching seminars and, most recently, her latest #1 NY Times Bestselling book, "You Are a Badass: How to Stop Doubting Your Greatness and Start Living an Awesome Life".<br /><br />She’s spoken on stages all over the world and has coached full-on super heroes, helping them build their dream businesses, become NY Times Bestselling authors, navigate million dollar business deals, find their soul mates and forgive their bitchy mothers who they now realize were just doing the best they could.<br /><br />Before becoming a coach, Jen played in several rock bands and eventually wrote her first book, a semi-autobiographical novel called, "Don’t Sleep With Your Drummer." When her plans to become a world-famous rockstar didn’t pan out, she decided to try being a lesbian instead, didn’t pull that off either, and wrote her second book, the National Bestseller, "The Straight Girl’s Guide to Sleeping With Chicks." Jen currently lives in New Mexico, and can be found on the web at JenSincero.Com.<br /></span>
